```
On Tue, 07 Nov 2000 15:38:19 GMT, Steve Thompson <sthompson2_@neo.rr.com> wrote:

>Warren Simmons wrote:
>> 
…[14 more quoted lines elided]…
>called CICS/TS or TS/CICS or some such. 

Nope, not correct.

<History lesson>
The father of CICS is Ben Riggins (IBM), and he headed a team of a few people (also IBM)
that designed and built a transaction processing system.  He was present at the last CICS
conference

He was  a  CE/FE  at  one  time and switched over to being an SE.  He was
located in Richmond, Virginia when he came up with the idea for what we
know  today  as  CICS.  His account at that time was Virginia Electric
Power Co (VEPCO).

When  Ben  was given  the  go-ahead  to  do  something with his idea, he moved to Des
Plaines, Illinois, which was the first development location for  CICS.

Initially,  Ben  reported  to a manager (Skip White) who really had an industry
responsibility and he really didn't manage CICS.   The  first CICS  Development or Product
Manager was Gerry Anderson.  Both Ben and Gerry have been retired from IBM for some years
now.

Among Ben's small group initially were Gerry Hughes, to whom Ben  gave the  responsibility
for the original master terminal (CSMT) and other transactions like that.  Carl Leinfelder
was given  Terminal  Control, John  Lawrence  had Program Control (and the introduction of
COBOL and PL/I support in 1970), and Ray VanderVliet had File Control.


It was later released as one of the first IBM program products.  In the original original
announcement letter (April 29, 1968) it was called PUCICS - Public Utilities Customer
Information System:


P68-66  4/29/68  Three New Type II Programs on Information Systems
                 to be Available Mid 1969

                 Overview
                   - Generalized Information System (Basic)
                   - Information Management System/360
                   - Public Utility Customer Information Control System

                 Generalized Information System Basic (GIS)
                   - Data set creation, maintenance, retrieval

                 Information Management System/360 (IMS/360)
                   - Implementation of medium to large data bases
                   - Teleprocessing and conventional batch processing
                   - Operate under MFT-II or MVT
                   - Highlights
                     - Messages to/from remote input/output devices
                     - Aplications scheduled concurrently under unique
                       storage protection key of OS/360
                     - System provides checkpoint/restart capabilities

                 Public Utility Customer Information Control System
                   - Planned availability
                     - June 30, 1969
                   - Overview
                     - Control system structure for installation of
                       electric, gas and telephone information systems
                     - Designed for inquiry and order entry applications
                   - Highlights
                      - Macro instructions for user communication with
                        his input-output devices and terminals
                      - Control programming services reduce programming
                        by the user
                      - Provides multi-programming capabilities
                      - Serviceability of system components to maximize
                        availability
                      - Records system performance statistics
                      - Uses OS?360 services

On July 8, 1969, CICS was born (Without the PU).  Also, it was announced as a class II
program (which means it was supposed to be free of charge), but when it came around IBM
made it a Program Product and charged money for it:

269-44  7/8/69   System/360 Customer Information Control System
                 Program Product (5736-U11) Ready for Shipment

                 Overview
                   - Data base, data communication interface between
                     Operating System/360 and user application programs
                 Major functions
                   - Task Management
                   - Storage Management
                   - Program Management
                   - Terminal Management
                   - File Management
                   - Transient Data Management
                   - Temporary Storage Management
                 System service programs
                   - Sign on/Sign off
                   - Master Terminal Function
                   - Supervisory Terminal Function
                   - System Statistics
                   - System Termination

                 Program Product Specifications
                   - OS/360 PCP, MFT or MVT
                   - Assembler language
                   - 2260/2265, 1050, 2740, TWX terminal support
</history lesson>






     With kind Regards            |\      _,,,---,,_
                            ZZZzz /,`.-'`'    -.  ;-;;,
     Volker Bandke               |,4-  ) )-,_. ,\ (  `'-'
      (BSP GmbH)                '---''(_/--'  `-'\_)



         Strike while the iron is hot.
```

```
latest) stop working on newer Windows.

by the Animator and the object code should be produced as .INT.  You may
need to force .INT format using OPT"0".
```

## Thread: Extracting data from .dat cobol files — 9 msgs

### Extracting data from .dat cobol files

- **From:** "Ed Regan" <ted.regan@virgin.net>
- **Date:** 2000-11-07T01:22:34
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8QIN5.81631$hk2.191638@news6-win.server.ntlworld.com>`

```
Our company has an antiquated stock control system that is programmed in
Cobol and is very old. I'm in the process of upgrading the system in MS
Access. I need to export the data files from the Cobol program into tables
in Access, but there seems to be no logical structure in those data files
i.e. they are not comman delimited or fixed width. I assume the format in
which the data is saved was upto the discression of the person who
programmed the original system. I have looked at the .dat files in a text
editor and they seem to have no immidiatly recognisable structure (although
obviouly they must have). It would be unpactical to manually re-enter the
data, as the customer file (cusma.dat) alone is > 20Mb.

There are no report features in the program, so I can't retrieve the
information this way. Also, the source code must have been lost in the sands
of time.

Does anybody know of a way in which I can get my hands on this data
considering I have no Cobol programming skills? Any help would be greatly
appreciated.

Thanks,

Ed Regan.
```

#### ↳ Re: Extracting data from .dat cobol files

- **From:** "Charles W. Cribbs II" <CHARLESCRIBBS@prodigy.net>
- **Date:** 2000-11-06T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8u7mg1$eke2$1@newssvr06-en0.news.prodigy.com>`
- **References:** `<8QIN5.81631$hk2.191638@news6-win.server.ntlworld.com>`

```
more then likely they are not delimited in any fashion.  cobol files are not
like just data files you open in wordpad or word.  they are not files made
for word processors at all.  depending on the type of files they can be two
associated files one being an index that will be unreadable to you and the
data part of the file.
your best bet to try to make they out is to use a product like transoft that
can perform queries based on the data fields.

you may have files that are random access, sequential, line sequential or
indexed.  the only one you will be able to read easily is the line
sequential.  you are going to have to figure out the record size and the
fields within the record before you can even design a table because if you
have the wrong data type you are screwed.
```

#### ↳ Re: Extracting data from .dat cobol files

- **From:** Vadim Maslov <vadim-nws@siber.com>
- **Date:** 2000-11-07T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A0895D7.918F9499@siber.com>`
- **References:** `<8QIN5.81631$hk2.191638@news6-win.server.ntlworld.com>`

```
Siber Systems has a solution that does it:

- We have a C++ library that can read Cobol data files and
  convert them to "regular" non-Cobol formats used in C++, Java, VB.
  It is called DataAccess.

- DataAccess can read indexed Cobol data files produced by 
  these Cobols: MF, FSC, RM, ACU, and sequential Cobol files
  produced by any Cobol program.

- DataAccess handles any Cobol usage and PIC, and it handles
  RENAMES and REDEFINES used in record description.

- A number of Cobol data file converters is built on top of this
library:
  - Cobol file to Flat file (CSV).
  - Cobol file to dBase IV DBF files.
  - Data Reader for Crystal Reports.

- Flat CSV (comma-separated values) files 
  can be easily imported into Access or SQL database.

- You can license both the DataAccess library and
  the specific converter tools.

- More details at http://www.siber.com/sct/datafile/

- You can start by sending us your data file for analysis.
  We can recorver the record description even without
  having the source for Cobol program that wrote these files.

Best regards,
Vadim Maslov
Siber Systems
```

#### ↳ Re: Extracting data from .dat cobol files

- **From:** "Russell Styles" <RWSTYLES@COMPUSERVE.COM>
- **Date:** 2000-11-07T01:27:01-05:00

```
    One approach that sometimes helps is to add a record to
the database with known values, ie "AAAAAAA" for first text
field,
"BBBBBBBBB" for second.  Use numbers like 1111111.11 and
222222.22
for numeric fields.  If you believe that the numeric fields are
packed or binary,
use a value that would be easy to spot in dump.
```

#### ↳ Re: Extracting data from .dat cobol files

- **From:** "Robert Kovacic" <rjk@bigpond.com>
- **Date:** 2000-11-08T10:03:08+11:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<AJ%N5.25216$e5.48355@newsfeeds.bigpond.com>`
- **References:** `<8QIN5.81631$hk2.191638@news6-win.server.ntlworld.com>`

```
When you say "there are no report features in the program" I presume you
mean there are no report generation facilities. For the system to deserve
the title of a "stock control system" it must produce many reports detailing
the Stock, Customers, etc.

Capture any of these relevant reports to a file, then write some simple
programs to extract the information from these files and write to whatever
type of data file you require. Of course you may have to capture the data
from more than one report to, for example, get the complete Product file,
but this is not complex.

We have been using this method successfully for the last 20 odd years to
convert new clients from their old systems to ours without requiring manual
data entry.

Regards, Robert Kovacic.
```

## Thread: Fujitsu Indexed File Structure — 4 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers) · [`VSAM, files, sorting`](topics.md#files)_

### Fujitsu Indexed File Structure

- **From:** floydj@netins.net (Floyd Johnson)
- **Date:** 2000-11-06T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8u6ft5$ent$2@ins21.netins.net>`

```
Is the specific file structure for indexed and relative files in Fujitsu
v.3 COBOL documented anyplace?  

I have glanced over the Language Reference and User Guide for help, but
could not find the details.  I am teaching a File Structures class and
would like to show students the underlying structure of the file.  For
sequential and line sequential files this is trivial.  Though I can
describe a theoretical description, it would be nice to give a concrete
example for the more complex file types as well.

Thanks for any feedback.

Floyd Johnson
```

#### ↳ Re: Fujitsu Indexed File Structure

- **From:** "Jerry P" <jerryp@bisusa.com>
- **Date:** 2000-11-06T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<tJLN5.238$EQ.159976@nnrp3.sbc.net>`
- **References:** `<8u6ft5$ent$2@ins21.netins.net>`

```
I once asked the same question of Realia. Their response was that the
blinding speed of their ISAM files was a competitive advantage and
they were reluctant to publicize their internal techniques - even so
far as to describe the layout.

You may have to settle for describing the old IBM ISAM techniques,
which are really pretty good for understanding the concept. More
modern methodologies, in my opinion, might get you so bogged down in
minutia as to obscure the basic idea.
```

```
character(s), and I then cannot animate the program any further. The manual
tells me to remove the numeric check, and I will not receive theRTS message.
```

```
028400                 IF (CUST-DGT(1) NUMERIC) AND
028500                     (CUST-DGT(2) NUMERIC) AND
028600                     (CUST-DGT(3) NUMERIC) AND
028700                     (CUST-DGT(4) NUMERIC) AND
028800                     (PART-DGT(1) NUMERIC) AND
028900                     (PART-DGT(2) NUMERIC) AND
029000                     (PART-DGT(3) NUMERIC) AND
029100                     (PART-DGT(4) NUMERIC) AND
029200                     (PART-DGT(5) NUMERIC) AND

029700                              W-WT1(WS-DIGIT-SUB)

029900                           ADD WS-PRODUCT TO WS-SUM
030000                     END-PERFORM
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: MF Personal COBOL for Windows

- **From:** "Leif Svalgaard" <leif@leif.org>
- **Date:** 2000-11-07T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<D3ZN5.642$ty.11558@typhoon.austin.rr.com>`
- **References:** `<8u9d9l$e9j$1@news5.svr.pol.co.uk> <8u9dk5$cha$1@news6.svr.pol.co.uk>`

```
if CUST-DGT has a numeric picture e.g. PIC 9, it is an error to
ask if it is numeric. You can only test non-numeric data for being
NUMERIC. The standard way of doing this is something like this:

02 CUST-ID.
    03  CUST-DGT     PIC 9 OCCURS 4.

02 PART-ID.
    03  PART-DGT     PIC 9 OCCURS 5.

IF CUST-ID NUMERIC AND PART-ID NUMERIC THEN
...

Bloggs <bloggs@neil-1234.freeserve.co.uk> wrote in message
```

```
> IF CUST-ID NUMERIC AND PART-ID NUMERIC THEN

I have never done it that way, always doing REDEFINES instead.

I don't care for this limit though - it should not be necessary.  A compiler can
be made smart enough to realize that if you are asking IF NUMERIC - the data may
be something other than numeric.  Or it may not be valid numeric packed or
binary fields - and make the required code to do the check.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: MF Personal COBOL for Windows

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-11-08T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8uca09$im7$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<8u9d9l$e9j$1@news5.svr.pol.co.uk> <8u9dk5$cha$1@news6.svr.pol.co.uk> <D3ZN5.642$ty.11558@typhoon.austin.rr.com> <3A09688D.7CC7031D@brazee.net> <3CeO5.3$G23.380@typhoon.austin.rr.com>`

```
FYI - The "new" VALIDATE statement (in the draft Standard) is explicitly
defined so that you may "check" whether a field defined as numeric -
actually contains numeric data.  (It also allows for several other "types"
of data validation - for the content of a data item matching the content of
that item.)
```

#### ↳ Re: MF Personal COBOL for Windows

- **From:** "Judson McClendon" <judmc@bellsouth.net>
- **Date:** 2000-11-07T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<rwZN5.6750$pj3.31131@news1.atl>`
- **References:** `<8u9d9l$e9j$1@news5.svr.pol.co.uk>`

```
Your problem is that you are lying to the compiler. :-)  When you use
a numeric PIC, you are telling the compiler that field is numeric,
but in your case, you're not sure.  If the field could possibly *not*
be numeric, never reference it using a numeric PIC.  There are a number
of ways to address this, but one solution is something like this:

    03  MY-FIELD-ALPHA.
        05  MY-FIELD-NUMERIC    PIC  9(6).

Reference MY-FIELD-ALPHA to test for numeric, then if it is, reference
MY-FIELD-NUMERIC to use it. :-)
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: MF Personal COBOL for Windows

- **From:** "bbrj66" <coboldr@netscape.net>
- **Date:** 2000-11-08T04:51:40+00:00

<a id="t-697cca74cf"></a>
## Thread: COBOL file extentions — 3 msgs

### COBOL file extentions

- **From:** David Essex <dessex@arvotek.net>
- **Date:** 2000-11-07T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3A08D6C7.12C247B2@arvotek.net>`

```
There appears to be several file extensions (.cob|COB .cbl|.CBL) used by
COBOL source files.

It appears that source files with (.cbl|.CBL) file extensions are
usually in fixed (1-80) format, while source files with (.cob|.COB) file
extensions are usually in free format.

Is this is a commonly accepted standard or just just a guideline
followed by some compilers ?


David
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL file extentions

- **From:** "Judson McClendon" <judmc@bellsouth.net>
- **Date:** 2000-11-08T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<16cO5.584$Ik.1382@news2.atl>`
- **References:** `<3A08D6C7.12C247B2@arvotek.net>`

```
"David Essex" <dessex@arvotek.net> wrote:
> There appears to be several file extensions (.cob|COB .cbl|.CBL) used by
> COBOL source files.
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> followed by some compilers ?

Most compilers expect .CBL or .COB, but there is no connection between
the extension and the fixed/free form of the source code, on any
compiler I know of.  You use compiler options to specify to the compiler
which form you are using.
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL file extentions

- **From:** "Leif Svalgaard" <leif@leif.org>
- **Date:** 2000-11-08T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<k05O5.1105$ty.28592@typhoon.austin.rr.com>`
- **References:** `<3A08D6C7.12C247B2@arvotek.net>`

```

David Essex <dessex@arvotek.net> wrote in message
news:3A08D6C7.12C247B2@arvotek.net...
> There appears to be several file extensions (.cob|COB .cbl|.CBL) used by
> COBOL source files.
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> followed by some compilers ?

this varies a lot from compiler to compiler.
You really cannot make any rules here.
```

```
This error at the command line that acts like a non-numeric error and kicks
the user out of the program.

Error: Insufficient memory for program, Program: ###, Line: ###

General: Old COBOL programs (MS Cobol v2.2)
	 Btrieve v5.00a
	 Windows 95/98
	 Novell Netware 5.1

The applications are customized set of DOS-based programs (over 200). The

program changes.
```

```
DOS=HIGH,UMB in config.sys should help a lot.   Take a look at what you

that you do not need.  There may be device drivers for CD's but you do
not access them in DOS programs,  simply remove them.

Does memmaker still work in win95.

Think about moving to NT,  they emulate DOS not actually run in it and
therefore give a huge amount for 'dos' applications.

Recompile for windows!!!

Ken
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: insufficient memory for program

- **From:** sff5ky@aol.comxxx123 (Sff5ky)
- **Date:** 2000-11-25T00:00:00

- **Message-ID:** `<20001125103628.17355.00001358@nso-fy.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<3A1FA956.DE2419C8@zip.com.au>`

```
In article <3A1FA956.DE2419C8@zip.com.au>, Ken Foskey <waratah@zip.com.au>
writes:

>bruce wrote:
>> 
…[37 more quoted lines elided]…
>

I don't suppose that you still have a setup preWin95 to check the environment
it was running successfully in?  How much available memory and what environment
variables were in place on the OLD machines?

MEMMaker is still on Win95, but is flagged for DOS-Mode only.

Not that this is the case, but I did on one occassion run into the situation
where the old programs assumed only 640K and the base  kernel and all
subsequent programs always begin loading at 640K down to around 597K.
In the load process the programs would check for a specific range.
When memory was below OR ABOVE this range, you get the infamous
Insufficient Memory message.

On your new setup, check how much memory is actually available.
Anything above 597K in the base 640K is suspect as a possible cause.
Try creating a LowMemory DOSPrompt, specifically requesting 600K
in the conventional memory section/tab.
```

#### ↳ Re: insufficient memory for program

- **From:** riplin@kcbbs.gen.nz
- **Date:** 2000-11-26T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8vpr2s$4q3$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<01c0562e$9afe1100$eeeb4d3f@Bruce>`

```
  "bruce" <bbarget@advdata.net> wrote:
>
> Error: Insufficient memory for program, Program:
###, Line: ###
>
> The applications are customized set of DOS-based
programs (over 200). The
> Cobol, we realize, is an older version but are not
sure if the upgrade
> would allow compatiblity with the current programs
and would cause major
> program changes.
>
> We have been experencing this problem for a few
years, since Windows 95. Up
> until then, we were running Btrieve 5.00a, Netware
3.1, and Dos 6.2 and
> didn't have this problem. Memory and speed of the
machines has not answered
> the problem. Some suggestions have been that we are
running out of the 640k
> base memory that you have to work with in DOS.

Yes. It is running out of base memory - the 640Kb
that DOS programs get to run in.  With MS-DOS 6.2 one
ran FREEMEM to optimise the OS loading to give
maximum DOS free memory in the base memory area - up
to 605Kb.  With Win95 this was hidden as MS tried to
hide the underlying DOS origins of Windows (extra DOS
utilities were on the CD but not loaded).  With Win98
the extra DOS stuff was not issued, with ME
(aledgedly) there is little or no DOS support at all.

> Any suggestions on fixing this problem or others
that have seen it and can
> steer us in the proper direction would be
appreciated.

1) Check all your CANCELs and reorganise the
CALLs/CANCELs to ensure that it is 'Last In - First
Out' to ensure that the maximum free memory area is
kept contiguous and unfragmented.

2) Check out the 'ON OVERFLOW' option of the CALL so
that at least it can close down tidily and without
data file corruption.  This _should_ take the
exception path when memory runs out so that the files
can be closed etc.  When files are closed set the
errorlevel and stop run, have the .bat file that runs
the system then do a restart using the ON ERRORLEVEL
to detect that this is required.

This may be a slow way to recover, but it might work.

3) Dig the FREEMEM set of files from the Win95 CD and
run it to maximise base memory.

4) Convert to MF Cobol and use XM to access several
megabytes of memory (expensive).  But at least MF
supports MS Cobol syntax.

5) Convert to another Cobol and ISAM file structure.



Sent via Deja.com http://www.deja.com/
Before you buy.
```

## Thread: help centering string1 into string2 — 9 msgs

_Topics: [`Help requests and how-to`](topics.md#help)_

### help centering string1 into string2

- **From:** goble@gtech (David. E. Goble)
- **Date:** 2000-11-25T01:23:30+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3a1f1334.22166110@news.adelaide.on.net>`

```
Hi all;

I have screen field display-action Pic x(80).

how can I move the text field action Pic x(?), so that action is
centered inside display-action.

ie display-action [bbbbbbbb]  blanks
               action [ xxxx ]
                result [bbxxxxbb]

I know I need some way to find the length of each string

I tried 

	function length display-action to lenB
	function length action to lenA
But I think my syntax is wrong.

I then 
	compute center=(lenB - lenA) / 2

How do I then position action into display-action.

I thought of something like

string display-action(1:center)  delimited by size
         action delimited by size
into display-action.

But this might be wrong too.

Can anyone point me in the right direction. 

I am using microfocus personal cobol.
--Regards       David. E. Goble
             goble [AT] kin.net.au
          http://www.kin.net.au/goble
Po Box 648 Kingscote, Kangaroo Island, SA 5223
```

#### ↳ Re: help centering string1 into string2

- **From:** "Jeff Baynard" <union27@macconnect.com>
- **Date:** 2000-11-24T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8vn7i00q01@enews3.newsguy.com>`
- **References:** `<3a1f1334.22166110@news.adelaide.on.net>`

```
Warning: untested code ahead...

ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
DATA DIVISION.
WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.

01  FILLER.
    05  DISPLAY-ACTION    PIC X(80).
    05  FILLER  REDEFINES DISPLAY-ACTION.
        10  DISPLAY-ACTION-ELE PIC X(1) OCCURS 80.
    05  HOLD-ACTION       PIC X(80).
    05  FILLER  REDEFINES HOLD-ACTION.
        10  HOLD-ACTION-ELE    PIC X(1) OCCURS 80.

01  FILLER.
    05  TBL-SUB           PIC S9(4) COMP.
    05  ACTION-SUB        PIC S9(4) COMP.
    05  LIT-COMP-1        PIC S9(1) COMP-3 VALUE +1.
    05  LIT-COMP-2        PIC S9(1) COMP-3 VALUE +2.
    05  LIT-COMP-80       PIC S9(3) COMP-3 VALUE +80.
    05  HOLD-LENGTH       PIC S9(3) COMP-3.
    05  HOLD-OFFSET       PIC S9(3) COMP-3.

01 FILLER.
    05  FILLER            PIC X(1).
        88  LENGTH-FOUND            VALUE 'Y'.
        88  NOT-LENGTH-FOUND        VALUE 'N'.


PROCEDURE DIVISION.
    MOVE <default-values> TO DISPLAY-ACTION.
    MOVE <action>         TO HOLD-ACTION.
    SET NOT-LENGTH-FOUND  TO TRUE.
    MOVE LIT-COMP-80      TO TBL-SUB.
    PERFORM UNTIL ( ( TBL-SUB < LIT-COMP-1 )
               OR   ( LENGTH-FOUND ) )
       IF ( HOLD-ACTION-ELE ( TBL-SUB ) =
                             SPACE OR LOW-VALUE )
           SUBTRACT LIT-COMP-1 FROM TBL-SUB
       ELSE
           SET LENGTH-FOUND TO TRUE
           MOVE TBL-SUB TO HOLD-LENGTH
       END-IF
    END-PERFORM.
    IF ( LENGTH-FOUND )
       MOVE LIT-COMP-80      TO HOLD-OFFSET
       SUBTRACT HOLD-LENGTH  FROM HOLD-OFFSET
       DIVIDE LIT-COMP-2     INTO HOLD-OFFSET
       MOVE LIT-COMP-1       TO TBL-SUB
                                ACTION-SUB
       PERFORM HOLD-OFFSET TIMES
          ADD LIT-COMP-1 TO ACTION-SUB
       END-PERFORM
       PERFORM HOLD-LENGTH TIMES
          MOVE HOLD-ACTION-ELE ( TBL-SUB )
                     TO DISPLAY-ACTION-ELE ( ACTION-SUB )
          ADD LIT-COMP-1   TO TBL-SUB
                              ACTION-SUB
       END-PERFORM
    END-IF.


That should do it.

Jeff


----------
In article <3a1f1334.22166110@news.adelaide.on.net>, goble@gtech (David. E.
Goble) wrote:


> Hi all;
>
…[36 more quoted lines elided]…
```

#### ↳ Re: help centering string1 into string2

- **From:** "DBuck" <dbuck@prairieinet.net>
- **Date:** 2000-11-26T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8vqtuf$5bcvq$1@ID-39920.news.dfncis.de>`
- **References:** `<3a1f1334.22166110@news.adelaide.on.net>`

```
There are lots of ways to do this.  Probably the easiest, code wise, is
this:

01    SPACE-CNT        PIC S9(4) COMP.
01    STRT                    PIC S9(4) COMP.
01    LEN                      PIC S9(4) COMP.
01    T-ACTION           PIC X(80).
01    D-ACTION          PIC X(80).

MOVE ZERO TO SPACE-CNT
                              STRT
                              LEN.
MOVE SPACES TO D-ACTION.
INSPECT FUNCTION REVERSE (T-ACTION) TALLYING SPACE-CNT
             FOR LEADING SPACES.
***COMPUTE STRT = ((80 - (80 - SPACE-CNT)) / 2) + 1.
COMPUTE LEN = 80 - SPACE-CNT.
COMPUTE STRT = ((80 - LEN) / 2) + 1.
MOVE T-ACTION TO D-ACTION (STRT:).

This assumes that T-ACTION is you test action field.  Since you did not
specify the max length, I assumed 80.  D-ACTION is your display action
field.

The INSPECT counts your trailing spaces within your test action field.  I
showed you the calculation in two different ways.  The first (commented
out), skips using the intermediate determination of the length (LEN) of the
text in text action.  The second is shown just to make it easier to
understand.

The idea behind it is this:  by subtracting the number of trailing spaces
from the maximum available space (assuming the text begins in position 1),
we get the length of the text within text action.  By subtracting the length
of the actual text from the maximum length of the display field, then
dividing by 2, we get the number of spaces we want to skip (rounded down).
Adding one gives us the start position we want...



David. E. Goble <goble@gtech> wrote in message
news:3a1f1334.22166110@news.adelaide.on.net...
> Hi all;
>
…[36 more quoted lines elided]…
> Po Box 648 Kingscote, Kangaroo Island, SA 5223
```

- **References:** `<3a1f1334.22166110@news.adelaide.on.net> <8vqtuf$5bcvq$1@ID-39920.news.dfncis.de>`

```

that you can inspect a function like this.  If it works when you
```

```
> certainly is supported in the draft standard.
>

While I didn't compile this particular piece of code, I have used
(extensively) all parts illustrated on an IBM390 using COBOL for MVS -
especially the FUNCTION REVERSE and the reference modication - which is
pretty much all there is to this little example....

Since IBM usually sits pretty much with the standard, I had assumed (perhaps
making an a$$ out of you and me, or at least me) that this was pretty
universal with the newer releases.  The COBOL for MVS that we are using is
from the early 90's.

Here is another example, using the same principle but not using the FUNCTION
REVERSE:

01    SPACE-CNT        PIC S9(4) COMP.
01    STRT                    PIC S9(4) COMP.
01    LEN                      PIC S9(4) COMP.
01    T-ACTION           PIC X(80).
01    D-ACTION          PIC X(80).

MOVE ZERO TO STRT
                              LEN.
MOVE SPACES TO D-ACTION.
PERFORM VARYING SPACE-CNT FROM 80 BY -1 UNTIL SPACE-CNT < 1
                                                        OR T-ACTION
(SPACE-CNT:1) NOT = SPACES
   CONTINUE
END-PERFORM.
***COMPUTE STRT = ((80 - (80 - SPACE-CNT)) / 2) + 1.
COMPUTE LEN = 80 - SPACE-CNT.
COMPUTE STRT = ((80 - LEN) / 2) + 1.
MOVE T-ACTION TO D-ACTION (STRT:).

Sorry if this is causing any confusion (although everyone is getting to see
several different ways to do this)....

Dave


> On Sun, 26 Nov 2000 06:01:28 -0600, "DBuck" <dbuck@prairieinet.net>
> wrote:
…[27 more quoted lines elided]…
> >out), skips using the intermediate determination of the length (LEN) of
the
> >text in text action.  The second is shown just to make it easier to
> >understand.
> >
> >The idea behind it is this:  by subtracting the number of trailing spaces
> >from the maximum available space (assuming the text begins in position
1),
> >we get the length of the text within text action.  By subtracting the
length
> >of the actual text from the maximum length of the display field, then
> >dividing by 2, we get the number of spaces we want to skip (rounded
down).
> >Adding one gives us the start position we want...
> >
…[48 more quoted lines elided]…
> My personal web site: http://www.geocities.com/Eureka/2006/
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: help centering string1 into string2

- **From:** "Ron" <NoSoy@swbell.net>
- **Date:** 2000-11-26T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<o5bU5.75$OL4.7326@nnrp2.sbc.net>`
- **References:** `<3a1f1334.22166110@news.adelaide.on.net> <8vqtuf$5bcvq$1@ID-39920.news.dfncis.de> <3a2128b5.47655251@207.126.101.100>`

```
Inspect function reverse....  works with the tallying feature.
I do this routinely to change trailing spaces to low-values to
make data compatible with goofy C stuff.

MOVE ZERO TO TALLY-FIELD.
INSPECT FUNCTION REVERSE (SOME-DATA)
  TALLYING TALLY-FIELD FOR LEADING SPACES.
MOVE LOW-VALUES TO SOME-DATA
            ( LENGTH OF SOME-DATA - TALLY-FIELD + 1 : TALLY-FIELD).

This works on OS/390 as well as Micro-Focus.

The obvious thought someone will have is why not do:
INSPECT FUNCTION REVERSE (SOME-DATA)
  REPLACING LEADING SPACES BY LOW-VALUES.
But this does not work. On OS/390 it will not compile. On Micro-Focus
it compiles but evidently the reversing action takes place in some work
area and the replacing action then takes place in the same work area
leaving SOME-DATA unchanged.
```

#### ↳ Re: help centering string1 into string2

- **From:** "Jason P. Hudson" <jason@44sycamore.freeserve.co.uk>
- **Date:** 2000-11-26T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8vrjlr$kts$1@newsg3.svr.pol.co.uk>`
- **References:** `<3a1f1334.22166110@news.adelaide.on.net>`

```
Hi David

I see you also use microfocus cobol.

A quick solution would be

77 WS-DISP-ACTION               PIC X(80).
            i would assume that ws-text is less than 80 chars long say 75
77 WS-ACTION                    PIC X(75).
77 WS-LEN                       PIC 9(02).
77 WS-OFFSET                    PIC 9(02).
.....
..
..
    *         get length of action text field and store value in ws-len
         PERFORM
            VARYING WS-LEN FROM 75 BY -1
            UNTIL   WS-LEN < 1
                 OR WS-ACTION(WS-LEN:1) NOT = SPACE
         END-PERFORM.
    *
    *            get offset - 80 been the length of ws-disp-action
         COMPUTE WS-OFFSET = (80 - WS-LEN)/2.
    *
    *            initialise the display field
         MOVE SPACES    TO WS-DISP-ACT.
    *
    *            move your action text to display starting at offset
         MOVE WS-ACTION TO WS-DISP-ACT(WS-OFFSET:).

I hope this solves your problem.
The use of refential access of individual charaters within a string ie with
the bracket + colon at the end of an identifier, simplifies character/string
manipulation and has been implemented in Microfocus Cobol.

Regards

Jason
```

- **From:** sff5ky@aol.comxxx123 (Sff5ky)

```
In article <8vm7ts$fp1$1@serv1.iunet.it>, "Stefano B."
<stefano.bottai@inf-or.it> writes:

>
>Hello,
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
>

I did not find ShellExecuteEx, but here is the setup for ShellExecuteA


      * ShellExecute

       01  HANDLE-TO-PARENT-WINDOW             USAGE HWND.

       01  lpOperation.
           03  lpOperation-Data                PIC X(20).
           03    FILLER                        PIC X(01)  VALUE C-NULL.

       01  lpFile.
           03  lpFile-Data                     PIC X(20).
           03    FILLER                        PIC X(01)  VALUE C-NULL.

       01  lpParameters.
           03  lpParameters-Data               PIC X(20).
           03    FILLER                        PIC X(01)  VALUE C-NULL.

       01  lpDirectory.
           03  lpDirectory-Data                PIC X(20).
           03    FILLER                        PIC X(01)  VALUE C-NULL.

       01  nShowCmd                            uns-int.



           CALL "ShellExecuteA" using
                            BY VALUE hWnd-HANDLE
                            BY REFERENCE lpOperation
                            BY REFERENCE lpFile
                            BY REFERENCE lpParameters
                            BY REFERENCE lpDirectory
                            BY VALUE nShowCmd
                RETURNING RETURN-VALUE.
```

```

Stefano B. ha scritto nel messaggio <8vm7ts$fp1$1@serv1.iunet.it>...
>Hello,
>
>1)There Is anybody with an example of use of ShellExecuteEx with
>   Optional parameters !!
>


The Solution !
..After much more time spent

      $set ans85 mf defaultbyte"00" case remove(beep) remove(escape)
      *SET ANS85 CHECK-CLEAR-BREAKS CASE
       IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
      *---------------------------------------------------------------*
      *           INF.OR. AREZZO  07.11.2000                          *
      *---------------------------------------------------------------*
       PROGRAM-ID. MARCO.
       ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
       CONFIGURATION SECTION.
       SPECIAL-NAMES.
           CALL-CONVENTION 74 IS WinAPI32.
       INPUT-OUTPUT SECTION.
       FILE-CONTROL.
       DATA DIVISION.
       FILE SECTION.
       WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
      *
       01  WS-Disp-Error.
           03  FILLER                      PIC X(23)
               VALUE "Extended Error Status: ".
           03  WS-Disp-Code                PIC +Z(5).
      *
      *
       78  SEE-MASK-FLAG-DDEWAIT      value h"00000100".
       copy "MiniWin.cpy".
       copy "WinTypes.cpy".
       copy "WinUser.cpy".
       copy "mfres.cpy".
       01 WS-ShellEx-Info.
           03 WS-ShellEx-cb           DWORD.
           03 WS-ShellEx-fmask        ULONG.
           03 WS-ShellEx-hwnd         HWND.
           03 WS-ShellEx-Comando      USAGE POINTER.
           03 WS-ShellEx-FileName     USAGE POINTER.
           03 WS-ShellEx-Parametri    USAGE POINTER.
           03 WS-ShellEx-Directory    USAGE POINTER.
           03 WS-ShellEx-Show         INT.
           03 WS-ShellEx-Histance     HINSTANCE.
      *Opzionali
           03 WS-ShellEx-IDList       USAGE POINTER.
           03 WS-ShellEx-Class        USAGE POINTER.
           03 WS-ShellEx-KeyClass     PIC X(4) COMP-5.
           03 WS-ShellEx-HotKey       DWORD.
           03 WS-ShellEx-Icon         PIC X(4) COMP-5.
           03 WS-ShellEx-Process      PIC X(4) COMP-5.

       01  WS-ShellEx-Return-Code     BOOL.
       01  LS-Shell-Return-Code       PIC X(4) COMP-5.

       01  WK-COMANDO PIC X(5) VALUE "open" & X"00" .
       01  WK-FILENAME PIC X(18) VALUE "C:\APPO\MARCO.RTF" & X"00".
      *
       PROCEDURE DIVISION.
       INIZIO.
      *
           CALL "COB32API".
      *
      * ShellExecute.
      *
       ESEGUI-SHELLEXECUTE.
           MOVE LOW-VALUE TO WS-ShellEx-Info.
           MOVE LENGTH OF WS-ShellEx-Info TO WS-ShellEx-cb.

           MOVE SEE-MASK-FLAG-DDEWAIT TO WS-ShellEx-fmask.
           MOVE 0                     TO WS-ShellEx-hwnd.
           SET WS-ShellEx-Comando TO ADDRESS OF WK-COMANDO.
           SET WS-ShellEx-FileName TO ADDRESS OF WK-FILENAME.
           SET WS-ShellEx-Parametri TO NULL.
           SET WS-ShellEx-Directory TO NULL.
           MOVE SW-SHOWMINIMIZED       TO WS-ShellEx-Show.
           MOVE 0                      TO WS-ShellEx-Histance.
      *Opzionali
           SET WS-ShellEx-IDList       TO NULL.
           SET WS-ShellEx-Class        TO NULL.
           MOVE 0                      TO WS-ShellEx-KeyClass
                                          WS-ShellEx-HotKey
                                          WS-ShellEx-Icon
                                          WS-ShellEx-Process.


      *
           call WinAPI32 "ShellExecuteExA" using
                by reference WS-ShellEx-Info
                returning WS-ShellEx-Return-Code
           end-call.
      *
           IF WS-ShellEx-Return-Code = ZERO
              PERFORM Get-API-Error  THRU Get-API-Error-Exit
              MOVE  LS-Shell-Return-Code    TO WS-Disp-Code
              DISPLAY WS-Disp-Error
           END-IF.
      *
       FINE-TRAS.
           STOP RUN.

       Get-API-Error SECTION.
      *
           CALL WinAPI32 "GetLastError"
              RETURNING LS-Shell-Return-Code
           END-CALL.
      *
       Get-API-Error-Exit.
           EXIT.

P.S. The        SEE-MASK-FLAG-DDEWAIT      Is used for resolution of
strange effetc of rtf openig file with Office-97 and the DDE messaging
parameters exchange !!!
(The motive of use of  ShellExecuteEX instead of ShelleExecute )

Stefano B.

Bye !
```

## Thread: Help: Trying to use ABEND-AID — 6 msgs

### Help: Trying to use ABEND-AID

- **From:** "CherylDCTX" <cymitch@flash.net>
- **Date:** 2000-11-26T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<KDaU5.16629$6W1.893967@news.flash.net>`

```
I am trying to use ABEND-AID to debug a program that has a S0C7.   I'm
not familiar with that software.  What is the best way to track down the
bug using this tool.  Do I need to compile the program using certain
options?  Is there a book/manual on ABEND-AID that I can check out?

Any help would be appreciated.

Thanks!
```

#### ↳ Re: Help: Trying to use ABEND-AID

- **From:** Alistair Maclean <LD50Macca@ld50macca.demon.co.uk>
- **Date:** 2000-11-26T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<OsbH9BAgGaI6Ewzb@ld50macca.demon.co.uk>`
- **References:** `<KDaU5.16629$6W1.893967@news.flash.net>`

```
In article <KDaU5.16629$6W1.893967@news.flash.net>, CherylDCTX
<cymitch@flash.net> writes
>I am trying to use ABEND-AID to debug a program that has a S0C7.   I'm
>not familiar with that software.  What is the best way to track down the
>bug using this tool.

Abend-aid is a formatted dump listing with diagnostics. The blurb at the
front of the dump will inform you of the locations within the program of
the instruction causing the abend and of the two items of data involved.
You take the address of the abending instruction and look up the table
of verbs and hexlocations in the compile listing (make sure it is the
correct version) for the instruction with the highest hexlocation less
than that provided by abend-aid. This will give you a line number to the
instruction in the listing. Look up and note the instruction and the two
data items involved. Now find the data items in the dump and note their
contents. That is how to find what data and instruction is causing the
problem but as to what you do to fix it and how it got to be full of
duff data is something else.

>  Do I need to compile the program using certain
>options? 

No.

> Is there a book/manual on ABEND-AID that I can check out?

Probably, but I've never seen it. If your site has bookmanager then you
may have the manual online. BTW, I learned all about dumps the hard way
with S/370 assembler, so abend-aid was a doddle to pick up. I guess that
to a newbie even a formatted dump is daunting but your seniors should be
able to provide assistance and guidance. Good luck.

>
>Any help would be appreciated.
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

#### ↳ Re: Help: Trying to use ABEND-AID

- **From:** mike__c@my-deja.com
- **Date:** 2000-11-27T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8vtl9g$t7t$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<KDaU5.16629$6W1.893967@news.flash.net>`

```
I think the previous replies may have been slightly misleading depending
on the Abend-Aid set-up in your shop. On any of the sites I have worked
in, I have only resorted to reading a dump by offsets when there were
problems with Abend-Aid.

At compile time, you need an extra compile step to add an entry to a
DDIO file. This will contain the source details that Abend-Aid requires
along with the offsets. AFAIK, this is also used by the Expediter tool.
There is obviously an overhead to having this additional step in
compiles, so many shops do not have this as a default compile option.

When your program abends, the dump needs to be sent to Abend-Aid. From
what I've seen, if the dump appears in your job, then Abend-Aid isn't
picking it up. A job is generally run at IPL time to tell Abend-Aid
which abends (by job name) to intercept, although this job can be run at
any time.

After the abend has occurred, go into Abend-aid from ISPF. In the entry
panel, the report dataset should refer to the dump dataset, and the
source(s) should point to the DDIO(s) from compile time. When you select
the failed job, Abend-aid will match the dump to the source (if
available).

From the 'output selection menu', I choose option 4 which usually isn't
listed as an option, and scroll to see the line of COBOL source, and the
field in error along with the bad data it contains (if an S0C7). Other
options let you check-out the contents of working storage fields etc.

If Abend-Aid complains that it can't find the executed source in the
DDIO file, it may ask whether it should use the most recent source or
let you select from a list, but this can give spurious results. If it
can't find a match, then you need to start looking at offsets as per the
previous posts.

If you have a system application support area in your shop, they will
probably have more details on how they've set things up.

Mike.

In article <KDaU5.16629$6W1.893967@news.flash.net>,
  "CherylDCTX" <cymitch@flash.net> wrote:
> I am trying to use ABEND-AID to debug a program that has a S0C7.   I'm
> not familiar with that software.  What is the best way to track down
the
> bug using this tool.  Do I need to compile the program using certain
> options?  Is there a book/manual on ABEND-AID that I can check out?
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
>


Sent via Deja.com http://www.deja.com/
Before you buy.
```

#### ↳ Re: Help: Trying to use ABEND-AID

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net>
- **Date:** 2000-11-27T01:13:58+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<qziU5.5776$1M1.852471@dfiatx1-snr1.gtei.net>`
- **References:** `<KDaU5.16629$6W1.893967@news.flash.net>`

```
At all the mainframe shops I've worked at, as long as you have if DD
SYSUDUMP in your job step that's where abend-aid's report goes (I just use
SYSOUT=*); but I do believe one or more of the CPU high priests and/or
acolytes need to set something up that says, "when a program abends, start
up Abend-Aid".

As far as compiling options: none are required, but....with your S0c7 (data
exception error), Abend Aid will report the BLW= and the offset of the data
and this data is available only if you get a compiler output list. (Which I
believe everyone does anyway).

You will also want to compile with "XREF(FULL)" so you get the
cross-reference of source code line number to code location; Abend-aid
reports the next sequential instruction at the time of the abend, so if you
have this listing you will be able to tell on which source code line the
program abended. There is some compiler option that will cause the O/S to
report this, too, but IIRC there's a real bad resource penalty for compiling
programs like this.

One other thing: check out www.mvshelp.com if you are doing mainframe work.
Very nice site.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Help: Trying to use ABEND-AID

- **From:** scomstock@aol.com (S Comstock)
- **Date:** 2000-11-27T03:56:22+00:00

- **Message-ID:** `<20001126225622.10648.00001818@ng-fa1.aol.com>`

```
CherylDCTX writes..

I am trying to use ABEND-AID to debug a program that has a S0C7.   I'm not
familiar with that software.  What is the best way to track down the bug using
this tool.  Do I need to compile the program using certain options?  Is there a
book/manual on ABEND-AID that I can check out?

===========================================================

Hmmm. I think people use ABEND-AID out of habit. Not necessary (and possibly
misleading) in these days of formatted LE dumps, I think.

Anyway, Michael Mattias replied:

At all the mainframe shops I've worked at, as long as you have if DD SYSUDUMP
in your job step that's where abend-aid's report goes (I just use SYSOUT=*);
but I do believe one or more of the CPU high priests and/or acolytes need to
set something up that says, "when a program abends, start up Abend-Aid".

====== in my debugging classes, we first turn ABEND-AID off.
====== this is done by including a DD statement like this:
====== //ABNLIGNR  DD  DUMMY

As far as compiling options: none are required, but....with your S0c7 (data
exception error), Abend Aid will report the BLW= and the offset of the data and
this data is available only if you get a compiler output list. (Which I believe
everyone does anyway).

You will also want to compile with "XREF(FULL)" so you get the cross-reference
of source code line number to code location; Abend-aid reports the next
sequential instruction at the time of the abend, so if you have this listing
you will be able to tell on which source code line the program abended. There
is some compiler option that will cause the O/S to report this, too, but IIRC
there's a real bad resource penalty for compiling programs like this.

====== No, the option OFFSET gives you the condensed listing, which is 
====== the correspondence between statement number and object code offset.

===== Compile with TEST(SYM) if you want something really useful; this
===== basically includes the data division map in the load module; this does
===== not create a resource penalty (although your load modules may be
===== considerably larger; however, there is no impact performance wise
===== until you ABEND, when this options will allow you to automatically
===== get a formatted dump of your data items: names you coded in your
===== program and their current values. This also gives you the failing
statement
===== number; again, no penalty until you ABEND, but then the resources
===== used are small compared to the trouble saved when you are debugging.

===== I am assuming you are using the supported compilers COBOL for MVS & 
===== VM or COBOL for OS/390 & VM.

<ad>
Check out our detailed course outlines for our debugging classes at our
website: http://www.trainersfriend.com
</ad>

Regards,


Steve Comstock
Telephone: 303-393-8716
www.trainersfriend.com
email: steve@trainersfriend.com
256-B S. Monaco Parkway
Denver, CO 80224
USA
```

## Thread: Parameter Passing Implementation — 2 this month / 13 total

_Thread started [2000-10](2000-10.md#t-de90b368e4)._

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Parameter Passing Implementation

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** "mangogwr" <mangogrower@telocity.co>
- **Date:** 2000-11-26T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8HiU5.44085$A2.8928717@newsrump.sjc.telocity.net>`
- **References:** `<8seuor$b0o$1@nnrp1.deja.com> <39eb2baf.1909435@news> <8sfmpm$qpr$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net> <39eb724e.19987901@news> <vP_K5.24900$Q8.5308885@newsrump.sjc.telocity.net> <8ti77o$djd$1@slb1.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
Actually, Bill, (and I could be wrong, but a careful reading of the language
ref leads me to think not)
I believe the method I described is the method ALWAYS used.
The only difference between By Reference / By Value / By Content  (And for
Ada
INOUT / IN / OUT) is  for non BY Reference, a COPY of the variable is made
and the
address of the COPY is used in the LIST, since in most Languages, a 'By
Value' or
'By Content' parm can be altered in the SubRoutine all you want, On Return
Linkage,
it is discarded.


On almost all Hardware, indirect addressing AKA Base+Displacement  IS
fastest.
All hardware has memory addressing and memory value moving restrictions,
and to overcome  these, the OS has limits and guides (see IBM's 4K paging
and its
impact on non-linear coding.).

In a world of Unlimited Stack size, the values could be moved back and
forth, but
it is and will always be more efficient pass the address of the data (even
when it is a
'BY VALUE' or 'BY CONTENT' copy), COPY the data to local storage, then work
on
the data and copy it back, than to try to store hundreds to thousands of
bytes on the Stack,
which after all, is only big enough to hold one complete set of registers.


William M. Klein <wmklein@ix.netcom.com> wrote in message
news:8ti77o$djd$1@slb1.atl.mindspring.net...
> NOTE WELL:
>   The attached note EXPLICITLY is talking  about ONLY "BY REFERENCE"
> parameter passing (even on the systems that it mentions).  This is (in
deed)
> the default if you don't specify anything else.  HOWEVER, on EVERY system
> (including IBM - where such things as "TCBs" are meaningful) - if you use
BY
> CONTENT or BY VALUE - you get VERY different parameter passing
"techniques".
>
> --
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
> > the default method is that for CALL 'xxx' using var1, var2, var3, what
it
> > does is:
> >
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> > Now, some systems add an address of all 00000 at the end (word4),
(32bit
> > addressing systems)
> > some systems (24/31 bit addressing systems) set Bit 0 of word3 'on'.
…[60 more quoted lines elided]…
> > > >the "data" itself on the "stack" - while BY CONTENT creates a
temporary
> > data
> > > >items and passes the address of the temporary data item.
> > > >
> > > >NOTE WELL:
> > > >  For this entire thread, as mentioned in one comment, it does HELP
to
> > know
> > > >which COBOL implementation and upon which Operating System, the
> question
> > > >applies.  Although the "semantics" of BY REFERENCE/CONTENT (VALUE)
are
> > the
> > > >same in all implemenations - the actual underlying structures may
…[15 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Parameter Passing Implementation

- **From:** scomstock@aol.com (S Comstock)
- **Date:** 2000-11-27T03:43:35+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20001126224335.10648.00001816@ng-fa1.aol.com>`

```
On Mon, 16 Oct 2000 15:00:00 -0500, "William M. Klein"
 <wmklein@ix.netcom.com> wrote:

This is BACKWARDS (sort-of) for BY VALUE and BY CONTENT.  BY VALUE passes the
"data" itself on the "stack" - while BY CONTENT creates a temporary data items
and passes the address of the temporary data item.

NOTE WELL:
 For this entire thread, as mentioned in one comment, it does HELP to know
which COBOL implementation and upon which Operating System, the question
applies.  Although the "semantics" of BY REFERENCE/CONTENT (VALUE) are the same
in all implemenations - the actual underlying structures may differ.
```

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<nf_T5.4953$nh5.390341@newsread1.prod.itd.earthlink.net>`
- **References:** `<6D7R5.24$i56.3018@nreader1.kpnqwest.net> <WfBR5.8391$n9.485645@newsread2.prod.itd.earthlink.net> <3a1a821a.79471293@news.eunet.be>`

```
Peter,
    The way we get the PID is via a C program that we link into the runtime.
When I get into the office on Monday I'll send a copy of the C program to
you via e-mail (I think its a one-line program).  Our session file is fairly
simple - We have a single key that is the user's login into our application.
While they are in the application we have the program keep this record
locked.  Then we read the file sequentially and whenever we get a "9D"
status, we know that record is locked.  We then store all kinds of
information in the record -- User's Name, date and time they logged in, PID,
current database they are accessing, etc.  Once the user logs out, the lock
is released on the record and the "old" data just sits out there.  I hope
this helps.
```

#### ↳ Re: MFCobol Client-Server

- **From:** Ken Foskey <waratah@zip.com.au>

```
NEXT, remember the primary key, read NEXT down another key, and
```

<a id="t-46e6e18c50"></a>
## Thread: Cobol Compilation Error — 1 msgs

### Re:Cobol Compilation Error

- **From:** peter_at_deja@my-deja.com
- **Date:** 2000-11-27T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8vtg7k$s7v$1@nnrp1.deja.com>`
- **References:** `<8uie2b$d9v$1@clematis.singnet.com.sg>`

```
In article <8uie2b$d9v$1@clematis.singnet.com.sg>,
  "Curious" <leng1@bigfoot.com> wrote:
>
> Hi,
…[41 more quoted lines elided]…
> >

>
Hello,

- metacobol formarly was developed by ADR and is now owned by CA;
  maybe that there are still manuales available, but products is
  was not more developed further since some years.
- by standard there are two output files from metacobol:
   DDNAME PUNCHF that contains the expanded (precompiled) source
   DDNAME LISTIN which contains an output-list with additional notes and
   errors
- rc 8 normally means a Metacobol Note, therefor search for 'NOTE'
   on the left side there should be a metacobol-message-number ;
   scroll right (line 80 - 133) there should appear two line-numbers
   the lower one should show you the line Metacobol doesn't want.
- to find out, where the LISTIN-Dataset is written do a TSO LISTA ST H
  or ask your TSO/ISPF-peoplem, how to chnage the generated jcl.

regards peter


Sent via Deja.com http://www.deja.com/
Before you buy.
```

<a id="t-71d22ecc3e"></a>
## Thread: 78 Levels — 1 msgs

### Re: 78 Levels

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-11-27T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8vve6s$deh$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<t1dofhpl9bvf73@corp.supernews.com> <74DR5.18451$qH.82256@news2.atl> <8v7k3a$e6v4$1@newssvr06-en0.news.prodigy.com> <8v7rcp$h63$1@sshuraaa-i-1.production.compuserve.com>`

```
Let's rephrase this a bit 78 levels (or data items with the CONSTANT
attribute that is being introduced in the next Standard) *may not* take any
run-time space.  The only thing that REALLY distinguishes them from 77
levels is that it is a "syntax error" (can be detected by the compiler) if
you try and modify them.
```

<a id="t-643299f385"></a>
## Thread: Fujitsu Cobol Report Writer 4.0 — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers)_

### Re: Fujitsu Cobol Report Writer 4.0

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2000-11-27T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8vvet1$gne$1@slb7.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<TMyR5.58935$a7.1070487@news1.rdc1.il.home.com> <3A177AB5.5378C447@siber.com>`

```
Or to be more explicit, the IBM mainframe compiler VAGUELY supports the '68
(not '74 - much less '85) ANSI Report Writer module with LOTS of "oddities"
(otherwise known as "bugs").  If you look on the web for SPC systems, they
have an "add-on" product that understands all the "peculiarities" of the IBM
OS/VS COBOL (and compatible) RW variations.  I am not positive that they
have a product for Fujitsu, but it is certainly worth looking into.

To the best of my knowledge, Fujitsu's compiler *is* conforming to the
ANSI'85 RW definition - but that will cause you problems (some caught at
compile-time - some not until you look at your output) if you are porting
IBM mainframe RW code.
```
